<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of <i>The Office</i> (U.S. TV series) episodes</h1>			<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
				<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>				<div id="contentSub"></div>
								<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Office_US_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="The Office US logo.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/The_Office_US_logo.svg/300px-The_Office_US_logo.svg.png" width="300" height="51" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/The_Office_US_logo.svg/450px-The_Office_US_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/The_Office_US_logo.svg/600px-The_Office_US_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="85" /></a></div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)" title="The Office (U.S. TV series)">The Office</a></i> is an American <a href="/wiki/Television_sitcom" class="mw-redirect" title="Television sitcom">television sitcom</a> broadcast on <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>. Created as an <a href="/wiki/Film_adaptation" title="Film adaptation">adaptation</a> by <a href="/wiki/Greg_Daniels" title="Greg Daniels">Greg Daniels</a> of the <a href="/wiki/The_Office_(UK_TV_series)" title="The Office (UK TV series)">British series of the same name</a>, it is a <a href="/wiki/Mockumentary" title="Mockumentary">mockumentary</a> that follows the day-to-day lives of the employees of the <a href="/wiki/Scranton,_Pennsylvania" title="Scranton, Pennsylvania">Scranton, Pennsylvania</a> branch of <a href="/wiki/Dunder_Mifflin" title="Dunder Mifflin">Dunder Mifflin</a>, a fictional paper supply company.<sup id="cite_ref-s1premiere_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s1premiere-1">[1]</a></sup> The series ran on NBC in the United States from March 24, 2005 to May 16, 2013. Additionally, nine spin-off series of <a href="/wiki/Webisode" title="Webisode">webisodes</a> of <i>The Office</i> have been aired on NBC.com.</p>
<p><i>The Office</i> aired a short <a href="/wiki/The_Office_(U.S._season_1)" title="The Office (U.S. season 1)">first season</a> in 2005 that consisted of six episodes. This was followed by a full-length <a href="/wiki/The_Office_(U.S._season_2)" title="The Office (U.S. season 2)">second season</a> in 2005–06 that consisted of 22 episodes, and a <a href="/wiki/The_Office_(U.S._season_3)" title="The Office (U.S. season 3)">third season</a> in 2006–07, with 25 episodes. Due to the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%932008_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike" class="mw-redirect" title="2007–2008 Writers Guild of America strike">2007–2008 Writers Guild of America strike</a>, the <a href="/wiki/The_Office_(U.S._season_4)" title="The Office (U.S. season 4)">fourth season</a> that aired in 2007–08 consisted of 19 episodes.<sup id="cite_ref-strike_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strike-2">[2]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/The_Office_(U.S._season_5)" title="The Office (U.S. season 5)">fifth season</a> aired during 2008–09 and consisted of 28 episodes. The <a href="/wiki/The_Office_(U.S._season_6)" title="The Office (U.S. season 6)">sixth season</a> aired during 2009–10 and consisted of 26 episodes. The <a href="/wiki/The_Office_(U.S._season_7)" title="The Office (U.S. season 7)">seventh season</a> aired during 2010–11 and consisted of 26 episodes. The <a href="/wiki/The_Office_(U.S._season_8)" title="The Office (U.S. season 8)">eighth season</a> aired during 2011–12 and consisted of 24 episodes. The <a href="/wiki/The_Office_(U.S._season_9)" title="The Office (U.S. season 9)">ninth season</a> aired during 2012–13 and consisted of 25 episodes. A total of 201 episodes of <i>The Office</i> aired over nine seasons.</p>
<p>The first set of webisodes, titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Office:_The_Accountants" title="The Office: The Accountants">The Accountants</a></i>, consisted of ten episodes and ran between the second and third seasons. <i><a href="#Kevin's_Loan_(2008)">Kevin's Loan</a></i> consisted of four episodes and ran between the fourth and fifth seasons. <i><a href="#The_Outburst_(2008)">The Outburst</a></i> aired in the middle of the fifth season and consisted of four episodes. <i><a href="#Blackmail_(2009)">Blackmail</a></i> aired during the end of the fifth season and consisted of four episodes. <i><a href="#Subtle_Sexuality_(2009)">Subtle Sexuality</a></i> aired during the beginning of the sixth season and consisted of three episodes. <i><a href="#The_Mentor_(2010)">The Mentor</a></i> aired near the end of the sixth season and consisted of four episodes. <i><a href="#The_3rd_Floor_(2010)">The 3rd Floor</a></i> aired during the beginning of the seventh season and consisted of three episodes. <i><a href="#The_Podcast_(2011)">The Podcast</a></i> aired near the middle of the seventh season (was previously available on the season 6 DVD) and consisted of three episodes. The latest webisode series, <i><a href="#The_Girl_Next_Door_(2011)">The Girl Next Door</a></i> aired near the end of the seventh season and consisted of two episodes.</p>
<p>The first eight seasons are available on DVD in <a href="/wiki/DVD_region_code#Region_codes_and_countries" title="DVD region code">region 1</a>, while the first seven seasons are available in regions 2 and 4. Starting with season five, the series is available on <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" class="mw-redirect" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray Disc</a>. This list is ordered by the episodes' original air dates and not by the <a href="/wiki/Production_code_number" title="Production code number">production code numbers</a> provided by NBC's official episode guide, which show the order in which episodes were filmed.<sup id="cite_ref-Episode_Guide_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Episode_Guide-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Episodes">Episodes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)_episodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Episodes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="Season_1_.282005.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_1_(2005)">Season 1 (2005)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)_episodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Season 1 (2005)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Office_(U.S._season_1)" title="The Office (U.S. season 1)">The Office (U.S. season 1)</a></div>
<p>Season one aired between March 24 and April 26, 2005. It originally debuted as a <a href="/wiki/Midseason_replacement" class="mw-redirect" title="Midseason replacement">midseason replacement</a> for <a href="/wiki/Committed_(2005_TV_series)" title="Committed (2005 TV series)"><i>Committed</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> It carried over general plot ideas from the earlier British series created by <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Merchant" title="Stephen Merchant">Stephen Merchant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Gervais" title="Ricky Gervais">Ricky Gervais</a>, and particularly the threat of wholesale downsizing. However, only the pilot was a direct adaptation of one of the UK version's episodes.<sup id="cite_ref-s1_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s1-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>This season introduced the main characters, and established the general plot as a documentary crew is recording the lives of the employees of the fictitious <a href="/wiki/Dunder_Mifflin" title="Dunder Mifflin">Dunder Mifflin</a> Paper Company. In a <a href="/wiki/Mockumentary" title="Mockumentary">mockumentary</a> format, it shows <a href="/wiki/Michael_Scott_(The_Office)" title="Michael Scott (The Office)">Michael Scott</a> (<a href="/wiki/Steve_Carell" title="Steve Carell">Steve Carell</a>), regional manager of the Scranton branch office, as he tries to convince the filmmakers of the documentary that he presides over a happy, well-running office. Meanwhile, sales rep <a href="/wiki/Jim_Halpert" title="Jim Halpert">Jim Halpert</a> (<a href="/wiki/John_Krasinski" title="John Krasinski">John Krasinski</a>) finds methods to undermine his cube-mate, <a href="/wiki/Dwight_Schrute" title="Dwight Schrute">Dwight Schrute</a> (<a href="/wiki/Rainn_Wilson" title="Rainn Wilson">Rainn Wilson</a>); receptionist <a href="/wiki/Pam_Beesly" title="Pam Beesly">Pam Beesly</a> (<a href="/wiki/Jenna_Fischer" title="Jenna Fischer">Jenna Fischer</a>) is trying to deal with Michael's insensitivities and flubs; and the temporary employee <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Howard_(The_Office)" title="Ryan Howard (The Office)">Ryan Howard</a> (<a href="/wiki/B._J._Novak" title="B. J. Novak">B. J. Novak</a>) is acting mostly as an observer of the insanity around him.<sup id="cite_ref-s1_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s1-22">[22]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span id="Season_2_.282005.E2.80.9306.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_2_(2005–06)">Season 2 (2005–06)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)_episodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Season 2 (2005–06)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Office_(U.S._season_2)" title="The Office (U.S. season 2)">The Office (U.S. season 2)</a></div>
<p>Season two of <i>The Office</i> premiered on September 20, 2005, and ended on May 11, 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-s2premiere_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s2premiere-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-s2finale_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s2finale-30">[30]</a></sup> NBC initially ordered only six episodes for the season, and in September, ordered seven more.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> On November 3, 2005, NBC ordered an additional three,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> and in the end it had ordered a full season of 22 episodes.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Season two featured the first "super-sized" 40-minute episode of <i>The Office</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-NBCRelease_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NBCRelease-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>The second season further developed into the plot of the fear of company downsizing, along with the introduction of new characters and developing some of the minor ones—especially that of Dwight.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> As Michael starts a relationship with his boss <a href="/wiki/Jan_Levenson" class="mw-redirect" title="Jan Levenson">Jan Levenson</a> (<a href="/wiki/Melora_Hardin" title="Melora Hardin">Melora Hardin</a>), Pam and Jim’s relationship become one of the focal points of the season. Their compatibility becomes more obvious as Jim’s feelings for Pam continue to grow, while she struggles with her relationship with the warehouse worker <a href="/wiki/Roy_Anderson_(The_Office)" title="Roy Anderson (The Office)">Roy Anderson</a> (<a href="/wiki/David_Denman" title="David Denman">David Denman</a>).</p>

<h3><span id="Season_3_.282006.E2.80.9307.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_3_(2006–07)">Season 3 (2006–07)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)_episodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Season 3 (2006–07)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Office_(U.S._season_3)" title="The Office (U.S. season 3)">The Office (U.S. season 3)</a></div>
<p>Season three premiered on September 21, 2006, and ended on May 17, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-s3premiere_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s3premiere-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-s3finale_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s3finale-55">[55]</a></sup> It featured 25 episodes, including two hour-long episodes, four "super-sized" episodes, and guest directors such as <a href="/wiki/J._J._Abrams" title="J. J. Abrams">J. J. Abrams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joss_Whedon" title="Joss Whedon">Joss Whedon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harold_Ramis" title="Harold Ramis">Harold Ramis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-s3finale_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s3finale-55">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>The season marked the move of main character <a href="/wiki/Jim_Halpert" title="Jim Halpert">Jim Halpert</a> from Scranton to Stamford, and also introduced <a href="/wiki/Rashida_Jones" title="Rashida Jones">Rashida Jones</a> as <a href="/wiki/Karen_Filippelli" class="mw-redirect" title="Karen Filippelli">Karen Filippelli</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ed_Helms" title="Ed Helms">Ed Helms</a> as <a href="/wiki/Andy_Bernard" title="Andy Bernard">Andy Bernard</a> (both members of Dunder Mifflin Stamford) as recurring characters. Helms would later be promoted to series regular. The main plot for the early episodes of the season deals with a recurring problem in seasons one and two—the problem of company downsizing—while in the last half of the season, inter-office relationships also became a major plot point.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, which assigns normalized ratings out of 100 to critics' reviews, calculated an average score of 85/100 based on five collected reviews, indicating "universal acclaim".<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span id="Season_4_.282007.E2.80.9308.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_4_(2007–08)">Season 4 (2007–08)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)_episodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Season 4 (2007–08)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Office_(U.S._season_4)" title="The Office (U.S. season 4)">The Office (U.S. season 4)</a></div>
<p>NBC ordered a full fourth season of <i>The Office</i> consisting of 30 episodes, which included five one-hour specials. However, the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%932008_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike" class="mw-redirect" title="2007–2008 Writers Guild of America strike">2007–2008 Writers Guild of America strike</a> shut down production for nearly five months in the middle of the season (between the episodes "<a href="/wiki/The_Deposition_(The_Office)" title="The Deposition (The Office)">The Deposition</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Dinner_Party_(The_Office)" title="Dinner Party (The Office)">Dinner Party</a>").<sup id="cite_ref-strike_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strike-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Because of the shutdown, the fourth season of <i>The Office</i> only consisted of 19 half-hour episodes, ten of which were paired as five hour-long episodes. The season premiered on September 27, 2007.</p>
<p>Season four marked the departure of Karen Filippelli as a regular character, although she appeared for a few seconds in the first episode, "<a href="/wiki/Fun_Run" title="Fun Run">Fun Run</a>" and in the sixth episode, "<a href="/wiki/Branch_Wars" title="Branch Wars">Branch Wars</a>", as the regional manager of the Utica branch. Relationships emerged as the main theme of the season, with Jim and Pam's rising, and Michael and Jan's, as well as Dwight and Angela's declining.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Technology was another theme as the office staff struggled with initiatives introduced by Ryan to modernize the company.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span id="Season_5_.282008.E2.80.9309.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_5_(2008–09)">Season 5 (2008–09)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)_episodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Season 5 (2008–09)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Office_(U.S._season_5)" title="The Office (U.S. season 5)">The Office (U.S. season 5)</a></div>
<p>On April 10, 2008, NBC ordered a fifth season consisting of 28 half-hour episodes,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> four of which were paired as two hour-long episodes. The season premiered on September 25, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>This season highlighted Michael's roller coaster relationship with corporate, as he is first praised and rewarded for impressive numbers despite the economic downturn. However, when a new boss is hired Michael feels slighted by his controlling manner. The theme of the beginning and middle of the season was mostly personal relationships with Dwight, Angela, Andy, Jim, Pam, Michael, Jan, and Holly. However, the theme transformed into career growth, as Ryan, Pam, and Michael set up the Michael Scott Paper Company, Pam and Michael go on a lecture circuit, Charles takes Jan's and Ryan's job, and Jim has trouble getting on with Charles. The last two or so episodes of the season focused on relationships once again, with major events taking place in Jim and Pam's relationship, and also with Holly and Michael.</p>

<h3><span id="Season_6_.282009.E2.80.9310.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_6_(2009–10)">Season 6 (2009–10)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)_episodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Season 6 (2009–10)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Office_(U.S._season_6)" title="The Office (U.S. season 6)">The Office (U.S. season 6)</a></div>
<p>On January 15, 2009, it was announced that NBC renewed the series for a sixth season, consisting of 26 half-hour episodes,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> four of which were paired as two hour-long episodes. The season premiered on September 17, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-season_6_press_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-season_6_press-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>Story arcs in the sixth season include Jim becoming co-manager with Michael of the Scranton branch, Michael dating Pam's mother, Dwight attempting to get Jim fired, and Dunder Mifflin facing an uncertain future due to rumors of insolvency, eventually becoming part of a larger corporation called Sabre. The season also prominently features the long-awaited wedding between Jim and Pam, as well as the birth of their first child.</p>

<h3><span id="Season_7_.282010.E2.80.9311.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_7_(2010–11)">Season 7 (2010–11)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)_episodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Season 7 (2010–11)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Office_(U.S._season_7)" title="The Office (U.S. season 7)">The Office (U.S. season 7)</a></div>
<p>On March 5, 2010, NBC officially announced that it had renewed <i>The Office</i> for a seventh season, consisting of 26 half-hour episodes, four of which were paired as two hour-long episodes.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Steve_Carell" title="Steve Carell">Steve Carell</a> confirmed the season would be his last on the series.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> The season premiered on September 23, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p>The seventh season of <i>The Office</i> largely revolves around the character development and departure of Michael from the series. After Toby is called for jury duty, Holly returns, causing Michael to once again pursue her, despite her being in a relationship. After eventually proving himself to her, the two get engaged, but Michael decides to move to <a href="/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado" title="Boulder, Colorado">Boulder, Colorado</a> to help Holly take care of her elderly parents. After Michael leaves, the office is forced to choose a new manager.</p>

<h3><span id="Season_8_.282011.E2.80.9312.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_8_(2011–12)">Season 8 (2011–12)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)_episodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Season 8 (2011–12)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Office_(U.S._season_8)" title="The Office (U.S. season 8)">The Office (U.S. season 8)</a></div>
<p>On March 17, 2011, NBC renewed <i>The Office</i> for an eighth season,<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> consisting of 24 episodes. This season focuses on <a href="/wiki/Andy_Bernard" title="Andy Bernard">Andy Bernard</a> becoming manager of the Scranton branch, before being replaced as manager by Nellie Bertram (<a href="/wiki/Catherine_Tate" title="Catherine Tate">Catherine Tate</a>) midway through the season. <a href="/wiki/James_Spader" title="James Spader">James Spader</a> also became a regular cast member, playing the role of <a href="/wiki/Robert_California" title="Robert California">Robert California</a>, the new CEO of Sabre. Also, Jim and Pam welcome their second child.</p>
<p>The eighth season of <i>The Office</i> largely centers around the antics of the new Sabre CEO, Robert California. Initially, he appears calm, collected, and calculating. However, as the season progresses, it becomes obvious that his management style is slowly destroying the company. Dwight—along with Jim, Stanley, Ryan, Erin, and <a href="/wiki/Cathy_Simms" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathy Simms">Cathy</a> (Lindsay Broad)—travel to Florida to help set up a Sabre Store, where <a href="/wiki/Nellie_Bertram" title="Nellie Bertram">Nellie Bertram</a> (<a href="/wiki/Catherine_Tate" title="Catherine Tate">Catherine Tate</a>) is introduced. Eventually, former CFO of Dunder Mifflin David Wallace buys back the company, firing California.</p>

<h3><span id="Season_9_.282012.E2.80.9313.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_9_(2012–13)">Season 9 (2012–13)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)_episodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Season 9 (2012–13)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Office_(U.S._season_9)" title="The Office (U.S. season 9)">The Office (U.S. season 9)</a></div>
<p>On May 11, 2012, NBC renewed <i>The Office</i> for a ninth season,<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> which was later announced to be the final season.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> The season consists of 25 episodes.<sup id="cite_ref-25epsnot24_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25epsnot24-203">[203]</a></sup></p>
<p>The ninth season largely focuses on the relationship between Jim and Pam Halpert. After Jim decides to follow his dream and start a sports marketing company in Philadelphia, Pam begins to worry about moving, and the couple's relationship experiences stress. Meanwhile, Andy abandons the office for a three-month boating trip, and eventually quits his job to pursue his dream of becoming a star. Dwight is then promoted to regional manager.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ratings">Ratings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)_episodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Ratings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div align="center"><b><i>The Office</i> : U.S. viewers per episode (millions)</b>
<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map name="timeline_88c7203e1b53a68cbf59cdff4f65c8eb" id="timeline_88c7203e1b53a68cbf59cdff4f65c8eb"></map><img usemap="#timeline_88c7203e1b53a68cbf59cdff4f65c8eb" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/88c7203e1b53a68cbf59cdff4f65c8eb.png" /></div>
<small>Source: <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_ratings" title="Nielsen ratings">Nielsen Media Research</a></small><sup id="cite_ref-s8-ratings_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s8-ratings-226">[226]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-s9-ratings_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s9-ratings-227">[227]</a></sup></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Webisodes">Webisodes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)_episodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Webisodes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="The_Accountants_.282006.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Accountants_(2006)"><i>The Accountants</i> (2006)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)_episodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: The Accountants (2006)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Office:_The_Accountants" title="The Office: The Accountants">The Office: The Accountants</a></div>
<p>NBC announced on March 16, 2006 that there would be ten original, stand-alone <a href="/wiki/Webisode" title="Webisode">webisode</a> shorts on NBC.com. They debuted on July 13, and concluded on September 7, 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup> They were directed by <a href="/wiki/Randall_Einhorn" title="Randall Einhorn">Randall Einhorn</a> and written by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Schur" title="Michael Schur">Michael Schur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Lieberstein" title="Paul Lieberstein">Paul Lieberstein</a>, and were edited by Michael Zurer, an assistant editor on the series. It took two days to film them,<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> and in June 2007, <i>The Accountants</i> won the Comedy Short Award at the inaugural <a href="/wiki/Webby_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Webby Awards">Webby Awards</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Daytime_Emmy_Award" title="Daytime Emmy Award">Daytime Emmy Award</a> for Outstanding Broadband Program – Comedy.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> In November 2007, the webisodes became a point of argument for the <a href="/wiki/Writers_Guild_of_America,_East" title="Writers Guild of America, East">Writers Guild of America</a> for <a href="/wiki/2007_Writers_Guild_of_America_Strike" class="mw-redirect" title="2007 Writers Guild of America Strike">the 2007 strike</a>, as none of the writers or actors featured in the webisodes were paid residuals for their participation.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup></p>
<p>Major characters Michael, Jim and Pam do not appear in <i>The Accountants</i> webisodes. Instead, the focus is on the three members of the accounting department: Oscar, Angela and Kevin—who appear in each webisode—as they try to find $3000 missing from the office budget.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span id="Kevin.27s_Loan_.282008.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Kevin's_Loan_(2008)"><i>Kevin's Loan</i> (2008)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)_episodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Kevin&#039;s Loan (2008)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>NBC ordered a new set of <a href="/wiki/Webisodes" class="mw-redirect" title="Webisodes">webisodes</a> for the summer of 2008. The webisode series began its run on July 10, 2008, and ended on July 31, 2008. The webisodes feature Kevin, who pursues a unique solution in an effort to pay back his looming gambling debts. The other characters who appeared are Oscar, Stanley and Darryl.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span id="The_Outburst_.282008.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Outburst_(2008)"><i>The Outburst</i> (2008)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)_episodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: The Outburst (2008)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>NBC ordered a new set of <a href="/wiki/Webisodes" class="mw-redirect" title="Webisodes">webisodes</a> for the winter of 2008. The webisode series began its run on November 20, 2008. The webisodes feature all of <i>The Office</i> characters except for <a href="/wiki/Michael_Scott_(The_Office)" title="Michael Scott (The Office)">Michael</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pam_Beesly" title="Pam Beesly">Pam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Halpert" title="Jim Halpert">Jim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dwight_Schrute" title="Dwight Schrute">Dwight</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Howard_(The_Office)" title="Ryan Howard (The Office)">Ryan</a>. <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Martinez_(The_Office)" title="Oscar Martinez (The Office)">Oscar</a> has an outburst in the middle of the office and his coworkers start an investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span id="Blackmail_.282009.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Blackmail_(2009)"><i>Blackmail</i> (2009)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)_episodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Blackmail (2009)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Creed decides to take up blackmail, and attempts to get money out of Oscar, Andy, Kelly, Angela, and Meredith.</p>

<h3><span id="Subtle_Sexuality_.282009.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Subtle_Sexuality_(2009)"><i>Subtle Sexuality</i> (2009)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)_episodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Subtle Sexuality (2009)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Kelly and Erin form their own girl group, Subtle Sexuality, and get Ryan and Andy to assist them with their first music video, "Male Prima Donna".</p>

<h3><span id="The_3rd_Floor_.282010.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_3rd_Floor_(2010)"><i>The 3rd Floor</i> (2010)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)_episodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: The 3rd Floor (2010)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ryan attempts to make a horror film titled <i>The 3rd Floor</i> using Dunder Mifflin as a location, and workers such as Kelly, Erin, Gabe, Kevin and Meredith as actors. <i>The 3rd Floor</i> was written by Jonathan Hughes, Kelly Hannon and Mary Wall and directed by Mindy Kaling.</p>

<h3><span id="The_Podcast_.282011.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Podcast_(2011)"><i>The Podcast</i> (2011)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)_episodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: The Podcast (2011)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Gabe attempts to record a podcast in the office about the Sabre website, hoping to impress corporate. The webisodes were made available on January 20, 2011 on NBC.com, but were previously included on the season 6 DVD release.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span id="The_Girl_Next_Door_.282011.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Girl_Next_Door_(2011)"><i>The Girl Next Door</i> (2011)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)_episodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: The Girl Next Door (2011)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The series focuses on Kelly and Erin's girl group called Subtle Sexuality. The first webisode documents the behind-the-scenes aspects of their second single "The Girl Next Door", while the second and final webisode is the music video itself, which features Ryan. The webisodes were made available on May 4, 2011 on NBC.com.</p>
